3.1.2  Business plan 
The URBIONFIN business model has a whole value chai n approach which integrates the business ambitions of the participant 
company partners including technology providers but also the bio-based products end users. 
Using CANVAS methodology the business plan proposed is detailed in further pages:  
Value proposition. Despite the improvements in sorting and recycling, a large fraction of Municipal Solid Waste (MSW) is still 
landfilled (31%) or incinerated (26%) across Europe . This practice is posing environmental concerns, a s well as wasting 
potentially useful resources contained in MSW. Comm ission adopted in December 2015 an ambitious new Ci rcular Economy 
Package . The revised legislative proposal on waste sets clea r targets for reduction of waste and establishes an  ambitious and 
credible long-term path for waste management and re cycling. To ensure effective implementation, the wa ste reduction targets 
in the new proposal are accompanied by concrete mea sures to address obstacles on the ground and the di fferent situations 
across Member States. Key elements of the revised waste proposal include: 
 A common EU target for recycling 65% of municipal waste  by 2030; 
 A binding landfill target to reduce landfill to maximum of 10%  of municipal waste by 2030; 
 A ban on landfilling of separately collected waste ; 
 Promotion of economic instruments to discourage landfilling  ; 
 Concrete measures to promote re-use and stimulate i ndustrial symbiosis  –turning one industry's by-product 
into another industry's raw material; 
 Economic incentives for producers to put greener pr oducts on the market  and support recovery and 
recycling schemes (e.g. for packaging, batteries, electric and electronic equipment, vehicles). 
Differentiating and enlarging the biomass feedstock  portfolio are key objectives of the bio-based indu stries in Europe. The 
abundance of sugars and other potentially interesti ng organic matter are identifying MSW as an alternative source of 
feedstock for the bioeconomy.  Exploiting MSW, one of many residual streams in to day’s economic activities, as a biomass 
feedstock source, contributes to these goals. At th e same time, utilizing MSW as a feedstock source fo r biorefineries helps 
realising the EU circular economy through industria l symbiosis, i.e. collaboration between producers t o use each other’s by-
products. The low economical value of state of the art recycled products from OFMSW like compost or bi ogas is limiting the 
sustainable implementation of separate sourcing sys tems since increasing citizen environmental (waste)  taxes is then need to 
tackle important logistic costs. New biobased produ cts can help to improve waste treatment environment al and socio-
economical sustainability .   
What does URBIOFIN offer? . URBIOFIN project offers a feasible integrated bior efinery technological solution that converts 
OFMSW into valuable bioproducts. This new Biorefine ry concept is composed by several integrated proces s technology units. 
The different interconnected modules that define UR BIOFIN biorefinery are showed in previous Figure 1. 3a. The biorefinery 
process units are adaptable to treat different MSW compositions, obtaining several marketable bioproducts as outputs. 
 
Table 3.1a  Targeted biobased products to be obtained at demo scale during URBIOFIN project 
Biobased product Use/ final application

Advantages . URBIOFIN proposes an economical and technical feasible technology for the conversion of OFMSW by:  
 New bioBased products portfolio, as well as technol ogy aligned with sustainability and waste EU-polici es that 
minimizes the anthropogenic impact to the environment, contributes to the European sustainable bioeconomy and 
adds value in reducing European oil dependence, improving the innovation competitiveness of involved industries. 
 Economical feasibility. More positive than the comp eting technologies (composting, incineration and 
biomethanisation). No need to raise citizen´s environmental taxes or at less extent. The business anal ysis show a 
Associated with document Ref. Ares(2017)2272851 - 03/05/2017
                                                                             BBI 2016-D6                                               
  
745785 URBIOFIN - Part B - 36 
 
 
rentability of the URBIOFIN model, current waste treatment technologies are profitable only with the application of 
the rate of waste treatment 57 . 
 Tailor made. Modular design projects for each clien t, covering the geographical, compositional and sea sonal 
variability of OMSW. Versatile. The different units  comprising the biorefinery can be adapted to curre nt MSW 
treatment plants. 
 Proven pre-industrial processes. The technical expe rience with the different demonstration processes u nits after 
URBIOFIN project realisation will prove a stable an d competitive biorefinery process at semi-industria l scale, 
ready for scaling up to industrial level.  
 The different units composing the biorefinery will be adapted for different market bioproducts demand and 
replicability of the biorefinery model worldwide. 
Market . URBIOFIN market has been analysed from two different points of view:  
- MSW Treatment market  for the Biorefinery technology (input of the biorefinery) 
- Bioproducts market (output of the biorefinery). The analysis of bioproducts obtained in URBIOFIN biorefinery was 
analysed in the corresponding bioproducts business cases (annexed). 
According to EUROSTAT official statistics, EU-27 co untries generated 239 million tones of Municipal Solid Waste in 2014 . 
Treatment strategies are identified based on report ed amounts of municipal waste landfilled (27.6%), i ncinerated (26.8%), 
recycled (27.6%), composted (15.9%)  and other (2.1%). “Composting” is defined in this statistic report as a biological process 
that submits biodegradable waste to anaerobic or aerobic decomposition  and that results in a product used on land or for the 
production of growing media or substrates. In 2014,  38 million tones of OFMSW were converted into compo st or biogas , 
24 millions more than in 1995. A continuous growth is shown over the last 10 years . In that year, average production was 
475 kg per capita (16% to compost and biogas) , ranging from 759 kg per capita in Denmark to 272 kg per capita in Poland 
and Romania. The variations reflect differences in consumption patterns and economic wealth, but also depend on how 
municipal waste is collected and managed. Globally  municipal solid waste (MSW) generation is approxim ately 1.3 billion 
tonnes per year and this amount is expected to incr ease to 2.2 billion tonnes by 2025 58 . MSW management in European 
countries has evolved over the last two decades fro m a focus on disposal methods to a greater focus on  prevention, recycling 
and valorisation. Moving municipal waste management  up the 'waste hierarchy' (i.e. waste prevention, p reparing for reuse, 
recycling, recovery and disposal) is a key way of e xtracting more value from resources while reducing the pressures on the 
environment and creating jobs. The global market fo r bioproducts  is expected to grow to $700.7 billion by 2018, wit h a five-
year compound annual growth rate (CAGR) of 5.5%.  The non-energetic market, the fastest growing segment overall, is moving 
at a tremendous 14.9% CAGR. The non-energetic biopr oducts category, which includes chemicals and materials, is the largest 
and fastest moving segment in this market and is ex pected to reach $472.8 billion by 2018, up from $23 6.3 billion in 2013 59 .  
The market size and current sales of bioproducts de rived from URBIOFIN biorefinery are described in ta ble 3.1b and more 
details appear in Addendum 1.

Existing alternatives. Current treatments technologies for OFMSW have been used for several years and are widely implanted 
technologies such as biomethanisation , composting  or incineration . These technologies are considered as substitutive  
competitors of URBIOFIN. On the other hand, there a re new MSW treatment technologies that can convert OFMSW into 
biofuels (direct competitors) (Figure 3.1c).  
 
Figure 3.1c Competitors of URBIOFIN: treatment technologies for OFMSW  
Out of all the MSW generated in the EU in 2014 (239  million tons, which correspond to 475 kg per capit a), 27% is landfilled, 
27% is recycled, 26% is incinerated, and 15% is composted 60 . 
Regarding direct competitors, there are several tec hnologies for the conversion of OFMSW into second g eneration bioethanol 
and bioproducts , which are all of them at demonstration scale. Som e of these processes have been developed by Bluefir e, 
Coskata, New Planet Energy or Fulcrum 61 . In these projects not only OFMSW is used as feeds tock, but also agroindustrial 
wastes. The substrate is firstly pre-treated by the rmochemical processes in order to make the cellulos ic component accessible 
to the cellulases for the subsequent enzymatic sacc harification step. Sugars -mainly glucose- are rele ased after the enzymatic 
hydrolysis and are then fermented to produce bioethanol or other intermediates. URBIOFIN offers a more complete exploitation 
of OFMSW resources.  
Customer segments. The main customers are the  EU  local authorities (municipalities ), which are responsible of OFMSW 
management. Statistics of MSW waste in the EU are o ffered in terms of kg per habitant or country as we ll as applied treatment 
(incineration, landfilling, composting or other). B ehind this data there are a large number of local a uthorities or municipalities 
that alone or creating consortiums of more than one  municipalities are responsible of MSW waste treatm ent. But, in practice, 
municipalities normally use owned public or private  waste companies to run MSW treatment plants. Access to building or 
exploitation contracts is only possible through pub lic tenders. There are two possible scenarios. In o ne hand, new OFMSW 
plants where URBIOFIN biorefinery approach can be f ully implemented, and existing OFMSW plants (produc ing compost 
and/or biogas) where all or one or more modules of the URBIOFIN biorefinery approach can be added to t he available facility. 
To have a successful business is key to integrate bio-based product end-users  in order to offer customers not only equipment 
for building-blocks or final bio-based products pro duction but also commodity/end product buyers. Desp ite the URBIOFIN 
consortium includes intermediate and end-users companies other end-users of similar profile are considered customers as well.  
Customer relationships. Access to building or exploitation contracts is onl y possible through public tenders  for building new 
OFMSW treatment plants, or renewing existing facili ties. Therefore, the consortium will invest resourc es (networking, visiting, 
tradeshows, etc.) to interact with public authoriti es and improve position and knowledge of upcoming t enders. URBIOFIN offer 
is of special interest for Public Procurement of Innovation  (PPI).  PPI occurs when public authorities act as a launch customer 
for innovative goods or services. These are typical ly not yet available on a large-scale commercial ba sis and may include 
conformance testing as in the case of URBIOFIN.   
Channels. Priority to apply in public tenders for building OF MSW plants is given to URBIOFIN participant compani es, specially 
to URBASER that implement OFMSW plants worldwide. B ut if this company refuses to apply, agreements wit h other waste 
companies (i.e. in countries where URBASER is not o perating) could be reached to increase number and q uality of channels. 
Networking with other EU waste companies is being c onsidered in the business implementation via techno logy licensing or 
specific agreements. A similar approach has been pr oposed for bio-based final products. Priority is gi ven for example to 
NATRUE to buy the produced cosmetic packages. NATRU E (project partner) represents companies from an em erging market 
in the EU. NATRUE has been – and continues to be – involved in different projects in the fields of scientific research/innovation 
and regulatory affairs where it provides expertise.  In this manner, NATRUE actively plays a key role i n addressing both

Key resources Most important resources for the business developme nt are project results and capacities and experienc e of 
the participant companies in the URBIOFIN consortium. 
Project results  at demonstration scale are key resources for the b usiness development: There are bioethanol and bioet hylene 
production, efficient production of new strategic a nd added value market materials coming from organic  matter residues like 
mcl-PHA, scl-PHA, biocomposites and biofertilisers, as well as data mining tools and models as well as  sensors and system for 
process control and engineering of the integrated URBIOFIN process 
In the other hand, the different project partners  involved in the project are in charge of different  units’ development in order to 
build the URBIOFIN biorefinery as a whole. IMECAL ( URBIOFIN consortium leader) will be in charge of th e business 
development and future commercialisation, having in to account the specific rules and IP protection of each partner that will be 
included in the Consortium project Agreement. The s pecific role of each partner in the business develo pment is summarized in

Key partners.  External partners to support the development of the URBIOFIN business will be invited to join the Advisory 
Group in order to get involved at the earliest stage of the business:  
 MUNICIPAL WASTE EUROPE is the European association representing municipalities responsible for waste 
management and their publicly owned waste managemen t companies, promoting public responsibility for wa ste 
management as a service of general interest. The members are national public waste associations and similar national 
or regional associations. They are committed to a s ustainable waste management that minimise the impac t on the 
environment and promote resource efficiency, taking  into account local conditions. Municipal Waste Eur ope promotes 
the interests of its members at European level, thr ough a joint position towards the EU institutions, and keeps its 
members informed on the latest EU policy developmen ts. The association encourages the sharing of infor mation 
among the members and the exchange of good practices in the local management of waste. 
 COPA-COGECA representing EU agri-Cooperatives to he lp market uptake of bioethylene as a fruit ripening  gas, 
agricultural plastics and liquid and solid fertilis ers. In 2013, there were 10.8 million agricultural holdings within the EU-
28. An analysis by economic size shows that among t hese there were 6.5 million (or 59.8 %) that had a standard 
output in excess of EUR 2 000. In terms of utilised agricultural area, France and Spain had the largest share of the EU-
28’s agricultural land, with 15.9 % and 13.3 % shares respectively, while the United Kingdom and Germany had shares 
just under 10.0 %. By contrast, the largest number of agricultural holdings was in Romania (3.6 millio n), where one

Business Case 2 It is studied the partial implantation of the urban  biorefinery into an existing MSW treatment plant, which 
already has a biogas and solid fertiliser units. In  this the modules are: bioethanol, bioethylene, VFAs, MCFAs, PHA, microalgae 
and aminoacids production units.  In this case the estimated plant investment is 10,950,000€. The expe nses are associated to 
the operational costs and amortization costs (10 years amortization time, 5% of interest). In this case the payback for the urban 
biorefinery is 2.5 years, and the ROI is around 55%.  
In any of the previous cases the reimbursement from  the waste disposal fees has been taken into accoun t for the business 
profitability. In case of including the profitabili ty of the business will increase, depending the tax  rate (50-90 € t -1 MSW). On 
average, the payback for the URBIOFIN Biorefinery  is 2-4 years . An increase in turnover often requires additional  staff. 
Based in the URBIOFIN plant business model and busi ness cases, around 135 employees will be created, i n particular, 8 in 
technological development and 15 employees per plan t with 8 projected plants in the next five years. 9 60 will be expected in 
2035. In order to ensure a successful market penetr ation, the consortium has identified the first end- user for the roll-out stage. 
The Eco-Innovative technological solution will be fully implemented at commercial scale in Urbaser installations and in 
Municipalities of ACRPLUS organization.

Implementation strategy.  
The implementation strategy of the biorefinery technology is based on the different points agreed in the Consortium Agreement. 
Each partner protected the IP of the demonstrated t echnology developed in the different Biorefinery un its. The implementation 
strategy needs to have into account the different points and actors for the technology commercialization plan development: 
1.  Create a specific multidisciplinary team  in charge of the commercialization Biorefinery tec hnology. This team has to be 
composed by people from the consortium companies wi th experience in the waste management, biotechnolog ical process and 
bioproducts commercialization among others. The com mercialization team will actively participate in th e communication, 
dissemination and exploitation activities of the UR BIOFIN project in order to reach potential clients that have interest in 
implementing the technology at industrial scale in the medium term (1 to 3 years after end of the project).  
2.  The main objective for the technology implementatio n is to build up the first industrial operation pla nt  to integrate the 
technology in the MSW treatment market. With this p urpose financing opportunities will be inquired (EU  financial opportunities 
for firt industrial plants, etc)  
3.  Develop a Specialist Company unit for the direct pr oduction and commercialisation of the technology, u sing the IP of the 
consortium companies in order to offer a complete and integrate Biorefinery solution for the OFMSW treatment.

3.2  Management structure and procedures 
3.2.1 Organisational structure and decision making 
Figure 3.2a shows the URBIOFIN management structure, which is explained in detail below. 
 
Figure 3.2a  Overview of URBIOFIN management structure 
The Steering Committee  (SC) will have the overall responsibility of the p roject and will consist of one senior representativ e 
from each partner. The SC will be in charge of comp lying with the Grant Agreement and monitoring proje ct progress against 
description of work. A SC meeting will take place e very 6 months and the Project Technical Assistant a ppointed by the EC will 
be invited to attend. During these meetings, the pr ogress achieved in the project objectives and in ev ery Work Package will be 
presented, whereas the work plan will be defined for the next semester. The Project Coordinator (IMECAL) will have a main role 
in the coordination of the board and in cooperation  with the other members of the Steering Committee w ill be in charge of: A) 
Content, finances and intellectual property rights definition (in close collaboration with the IPR Man ager (BCM)) A.1) Collection 
of financial information from the partners and the provision of regular periodic reports to the BBI JU . A.2) Changes/setting up to 
the Consortium Agreement. A.3). Looking for the pro per potential investors in closed collaboration wit h the Exploitation 
Manager (BCM), interested in the project results. B ) Organization of all Consortium meetings, Review M eetings and events. C) 
Evolution of the Consortium. D) Discussion and solv ing of business and technical problems that may ari se in conjunction with 
the Scientific and Technical Committee, Innovation Committee and Business Committee. The SC will take decisions towards 
mitigation of risks that might jeopardize the effective progress of the project. E) Monitoring of results and establishment contacts 
with other relevant projects, clusters or initiativ es (include samples related to objectives of the pr oject). F) Developing the 
project dissemination and exploitation strategy und er the hat of the Exploitation, Communication and D issemination Manager. 
Each Member of the SC has one vote. 
The Project Coordinator  (PC) will be responsible for the administrative, f inancial and organizational management of the 
project as a whole and will be the point of contact  with the BBI JU. In URBIOFIN, the project coordina tor will be IMECAL, 
represented by Ms Caterina Coll. She has extensive knowledge and expertise in the area of EU funding a nd project 
management and relevant expertise in the field of W aste Management and Renewable Technologies. Additio nally, at the start 
of the project, a Financial Manager from the coordi nating organisation will be assigned to support the  project coordinator in the 
project coordination. The Project Coordinator shall  have as responsibilities: A) Overall responsibilit y for the project; guarantees 
its continuity and consistency and allocates its resources adequately. B) Handles any conflict resolution within the project, which 
could not be handled at a lower level. C) Monitors compliance by the parties with their obligations. D ) Keeps the address list of 
members and other contact persons updated and available. E) Collects, reviews and submits information on the progress of the 
project and reports and other deliverables (including financial statements and related certification) to the BBI JU. F) Acts as the 
speaker of the project in all interactions with the  EC and third parties. G) Consolidates the project planning, milestones reports, 
BBI JU  
Associated with document Ref. Ares(2017)2272851 - 03/05/2017
                                                                             BBI 2016-D6                                               
  
745785 URBIOFIN - Part B - 44 
 
 
cost statements and budget. H) Communicates with wo rk packages in order to guarantee smooth progress a nd avoid delays in 
deliverables and milestones. The PC will act to mit igate the impact caused for these potential delays.  If these issues are not 
resolved satisfactorily, these will be raised with the SC. I) Transmits promptly documents, minutes of  the Steering Committee, 
Scientific and Technical Committee, Innovation Comm ittee and Business Committee and information connec ted with the 
project. J) Monitors the implementation of decisions taken at consortium, SC, S&TC, IC and BC meetings. 
The Scientific & Technical Committee (S&TC)  will be responsible for the technical progress of the project; it will comprise the 
leaders of each technical work package and will be chaired by AINIA. In close collaboration with the S &T Manager the 
Validation Manager (URBASER) will be responsible fo r ensuring a successful demonstration and validatio n of the innovative 
solutions. The S&TC will have significant role and will be responsible for the coordination of the tec hnical aspects of the project 
and the proper identification of all interfaces. At  management level, the main role of the S&TC will b e to identify effective 
technical risk management in close collaboration wi th the Risk Manager (EXERGY); means for follow up t he technical 
achievements in the project and for technical decis ion support. The chair of the S&TC will organize te chnical meetings every 3 
months with the cooperation of the work-package lea ders. The main tasks of the S&TC are: A) Responsibl e for technical and 
scientific progress of the project and for completi ng successfully the S&T objectives and activities o f the project in a timely 
manner. B) Responsible for the adequate focus and c o-ordination of technical work within the consortiu m. C) Provide links of 
the project with other efforts, projects and overal l initiatives that are related to the theme of the project either from within the 
enterprises or outside of the enterprises at a nati onal or international level. D) When necessary, e.g . due to a technological 
breakthrough, adjusts the content and direction of research. E) Identify possible technical problems a nd conflicts between the 
WPs that may restrain the projects technical evolut ion and will convoke a meeting for their resolution  F) The S&TC is expected 
to meet in average 4 times a year. Telephone and we b meetings will be used complementary to the physic al meetings for 
keeping close track to the development of the subpr ojects. At the S&TC Meetings the WP Leaders will re port the work status 
following the decision taking procedure established . The S&T Manager can request an urgent Steering Co mmittee meeting to 
the Project Coordinator in case a strategic decision related to a Scientific or technical matter has to be made. 
The Innovation Committee (IC)  will be responsible for increasing of the innovation level in the consortium, in RTD activities, in 
the business models, with a consequent harmonisatio n of the whole project management; it will comprise  representative of 
each partner and will be chaired by EXERGY. The Inn ovation Manager (IM) will be responsible for advisi ng the SC on 
contingency implementation. EXERGY will assist the PC in managing risk across the partnership and work  packages. This will 
include maintenance of the risk table as well as the implementation of approved contingency actions. In close collaboration with 
the IC Manager, the Exploitation, Dissemination & C ommunication Manager (ED&CM) represented by BCM, as  major 
orchestrator of the internal processes of project m anagement will have three main roles: A) The ED&CM will contribute 
developing and managing the dissemination strategy,  monitoring the results and establishing contacts w ith other relevant 
project. Moreover, the ED&CM manager will be in charge for the organisation of Workshops, conferences, training sessions and 
other events relevant to project promotion. B) As r esponsible of exploitation strategy, the ED&CM will manage the promotion of 
the solutions developed during the project. The ED& CM will look for potential stakeholders and investo rs, interested in the 
project results, and will be constantly in contact with the public administration, to promote follow-u p activities. C) In charge for 
Knowledge management and Intellectual Property Righ ts, the ED&CM will be available for discussions reg arding IPR with the 
partners at any time during the project. To avoid t he creation of conflicts with regard to rights of u se and commercialisation of 
certain IPR arising from the project, the partners will, during the negotiation of the grant agreement , conduct due diligence to 
determine whether any partner has pre-existing obli gations with respect to specific IPR. Intellectual Property Rights (IPR) is a 
major management issue in the exploitation and dissemination of scientific project results. Once a year, the Innovation Manager 
and the ED&CM will assemble the SC. Together, they will review the results generated by the project an d update the 
exploitation plan. The management of IPR will involve: a) Identification of patentable research findings b) Evaluation of whether 
to file for IPR protection or not c) Preparation of  applications for IPR protection d) Determination o f the rights of use for each 
single Innovative solution of the URBIOFIN project e) Exploitation of the IPR generated by the partners.  
The Business Committee (BC)  will be responsible for developing a business stra tegy to take the project results closer to 
market including the identification of post project  funding needs and funding opportunities. It will c omprise representative of 
each partner and will be chaired by IMECAL, who will lead on the development of the commercialisation strategy in consultation 
with the different stakeholders within the consorti um in order to facilitate commercial exploitation b y the ED&CM. The BC will 
meet once a year to review the SC results generated by the project and update the business plan.  
The Advisory Board  constitutes a consultation body that will comprise  well-reputed experts in the sector of waste 
management, biomaterials, as well as municipalities ’ representatives. Its purpose is to provide advice  and guidance to the 
project. Furthermore, the Advisory Board will ensur e that the project management is constantly informe d of significant changes 
in the knowledge domains and markets underpinning t he project activities. The Advisory Board will oper ate mostly remotely in 
so called Virtual Joint Sessions exploiting teleconference facilities and/or via (e-) mail based interaction, but it will meet possibly

at least three times in the project life span (at the beginning: M3, mid-way through: M24 and at the end: M48) by arrangement at 
venues to be agreed by members with the coordinating party in the composition that would most fit the needs of the meeting. 
The WP leaders (WPL) will be in charge of the imple mentation of the R&D activities at the WP level. The WPLs will be 
responsible for the coordination, planning, and monitoring of their work packages, i.e. they will coordinate the activities between 
the different partners collaborating on that WP and  facilitate information exchange. Every WPL will al so examine the 
deliverables provided by the partners from his/her WP and insure that they are produced with the appro priate quality, on time 
and according to the budget. The WPLs will hold tel econferences as required with the PC, the SC and th e S&TM. In summary, 
their main roles will be: A) To manage the scientific and technical advancement of the WPs. B) To report and prepare proposals 
for the S&TM considering S&T aspects and to report and prepare proposals for the SC with regard to the  achievements of the 
work plan and major budget allocations. 
3.2.2 Innovation management 
As URBIOFIN is a project with ambitious technologic al aims, the consortium needs to be ensured that in  4 years’ time the 
solution will still correspond to the market needs and represent an innovative technological approach,  successfully replicated 
and demonstrated. To achieve this, the URBIOFIN con sortium shall make effort to understand and face bo th market and 
technical problems. The management strategy is reco gnized as a key factors for succeed in this aspect.  Therefore, a special 
attention will be given to the following main managerial aspects (efforts are calculated for all of them in the budget):  
- At innovation and market side : A) A large industrial network will be brought to the consortium and project results in order to 
be sure that a leading market solution could be pro vided not more than 1 year period after the project end. For this purpose the 
consortium set-up 2 consultative bodies that shall ensure the project innovation, test the solution an d provide additional 
requirements and know-how related to their own busi ness processes. The consultative bodies are represe nted by the 
Innovation Committee and the Business Committee. B)  Clear business plan and ownership rights agreement  set-up still at the 
project beginning. C) A separate Exploitation Manager (BCM) experience in companies’ creation and business development will 
support the team during the entire project life-cycle.  
- At technical side : A) Requirements managements methodology set up from the project beginning: the experience achieved in 
large scaled research and innovation projects shows  a clear need to identify method for ensuring the r equirements 
management and proper validation when interdiscipli nary research. It shall be specific for the project  objectives but not 
consuming a lot of personnel efforts as standard re quirements engineering methods. B) Set-up an integr ation plan with respect 
to the interfaces management: follow up of the inte rfaces and setting up a plan with maturity levels f or achievements for the 
entire solution integration will lead to a better cooperation, reporting among partners and objective oriented decisions-taken.
3.3  Consortium as a whole 
The project consortium includes 16 partners from 8 countries worldwide at almost all relevant levels (industrial, scientific and 
agricultural sectors) with broad and diverse wealth of experience of project partners and associated partners to allow co-creation 
(multi-actor approach ). The integration of 8 countries into the project enables a widespread and country-specific view on t he 
handling of MSW as well as about market strategies from different approaches. All consortium partners have extensive 
experience in European and international programmes  and projects (see Table 1.3b and section 4). They are experienced in 
working efficiently within a consortium and will br ing specific and complementary expertise. The conso rtium includes partners 
from research organisations, and academic sector combined with a high share of SME and industrial sector. 10 from 16 project 
partners are involved as SME/industrial  project partner with a share of total budget of ap prox 50%, as well as the leader is a 
SME partner. The industrial partners are involved t o support the selected innovative approaches, to gi ve technical assessment, 
to support the further technological development, to implement the project results and to support their marketability.  
The consortium is well equipped to work together to  develop different work packages and to secure the commitment for the 
implementation of the joint activities. 6 of eight work packages will be organised by femal e WP leader (see paragraph 
1.3.5 ). All parties will contribute to the project in a meaningful way and ensure that the geographical spr ead will be beneficial for 
the impact and sustainability of the collaboration and coordination of research programmes in Europe a nd abroad. Table 3.3a 
describes the involved project partners and their main tasks within the project.

AINIA 
Ainia will be focused in the development of two pha se AD systems and in the VFA valorisation throughou t the conversion 
of VFA to MCFA and later into PHA. Moreover it will  participate in the valorisation of microalgae to b iofertiliser. Ainia will 
participate in almost all WP, except WP2. 
URBASER 
URBASER will offer its R&D Center area to install n ew prototypes or pilot plants which allow the opera tion and validation 
of innovative technological solutions for the treatment of outlet streams coming from the fermentation  process of municipal 
solid wastes, in order to get as much of high-grade  valuable products (biopolymers, biomethane, microa lgae) and 
maximize the valorisation of the organic fraction o f MSW (OFMSW). In particular, URBASER will particip ate in the 
anaerobic digestion of OFMSW for VFA production and  biogas production through methanogenic steps (WP3,  WP4), 
operating its anaerobic digester according to the p roject needs. Furthermore, Urbaser will integrate o f VFA, PHA 
production and microalgae processes.   
BPE 
Role of BIOMASA includes the participation in the f ollowing WPs: 1, 4, 5, 6, 7 and 8, being related to  biofertilisers 
development from organic fraction and microalgae ex tracts, under the form of solid and liquid by-produ cts from down-
stream units of Fermentation, AD and Biomethane upg rading. Experimental formulation, legal and technic al evaluation, as 
well as demonstration and dissemination activities. 
UVA 
The EnvTech group will be involved in the upgrading  of raw biogas to biomethane in photobioreactors, t he selective 
removal of siloxanes from biomethane in two phase p artitioning bioreactors, the selective removal of H 2S from biogas and 
its further bioconversion into high-added value pro ducts such as PHAs. EnvTech will apply its 16 years  of R&D 
experience in the design and operation of algal-bac terial photobioreactors to optimize the upgrading p otential and 
maximize the production of biobased products. The g roup has successfully operated both open and enclos ed 
photobioreactors under indoor and outdoor condition s for the treatment of domestic and livestock waste waters. Besides, 
the broad experience of the EnvTech group in the op eration of low-cost, high-efficiency bioreactors fo r waste gas 
treatment will be applied to the selective removal of siloxanes and H 2S, and to the bioconversion of the raw biogas to 
high-added value products.  
EXERGY 
Exergy leads the WP6 where the entire urban process  will be integrated and optimised through virtual s imulations as well 
as the project’s impacts will be assessed (economic , environmental and social) along with the study of  all the potential 
regulatory and legal aspects which might impact on the project outcomes. 
NOVO 
Novozymes will sample enzyme products optimized for  degradation of MSW and provide recommendations for  
optimization of enzyme application in the Perseo Bi oethanol® process to enable cost-efficient conversi on of MSW to 
sugars for further downstream processing into higher-value products. 
GID 
G.I. Dynamics aims to be partner in the Project by designing and building a pilot plant downstream of the produced 
ethanol. The pilot plant will produce Ethylene up t o Polyethylene, with a goal to validate that the pr oduced ethanol is 
suitable for sustainable ethylene derivative chemicals. 
WR 
Wageningen Research will establish fermentation pro cesses using Cryptococcus sp.  for medium-chain fatty acid (MCFA) 
based on the existing volatile fatty acid (VFA) str eam and will establish a fermentation process for m cl-PHA production 
using the MCFA’s as substrate and exiting mixed cul tures and/or pure cultures of Pseudomonas putida  as production 
organism. In addition, WR will be responsible for f ormulating/developing novel composites based on the  biomaterials 
deriving from MSW (pulp, mcl-PHA, scl-PHA). 
CIEMAT 
CIEMAT will be focused on adapting/improving the PE RSEO bioethanol production process to the new feeds tock by 
optimizing pretreatment, enzymatic hydrolysis and f ermentation steps. Apart from sugar recovery and et hanol yield, 
energy efficiency ratio, mass balance and toxic com pounds generation will be used for the estimation o f the optimized 
parameters. CIEMAT will also assist IMECAL in the analysis of the fractions generated in the demo trials. 
VISUM 
VISUM will participate in WP2 where they will test novel advanced sensors for monitoring selected proc ess parameters 
and will integrate them at plant level together wit h a bespoke control system. They will also collabor ate in the study of the 
relevant parameters to select the most suitable sen sor technologies. They will also develop data minin g tools to produce 
relevant decision support tools for optimally contr olling production based on relevant process data. V ISUM will also 
participate in WP1, supporting the work on prelimin ary actions for biorefinery design which will feed into WP2. VISUM will 
also take part in WP6, in the environmental, econom ic and regulatory assessments from the monitoring a t plant scale 
point of view and will participate in WP7 by actively engaging in exploitation and dissemination tasks. 
NATURE 
PLAST 
Natureplast’s role will mainly be focused on charac terizing the raw polymers (PHA) produced by the con sortium, and to 
modify them to improve their processability and properties for the targeted applications. 
IRIAF / 
GEACAM 
IRIAF / GEACAM will be in charge of the VFA valoris ation throughout the conversion of VFA to MCFA and later into PHA 
in a demonstrative scale (bioreactor of 20 m 3). Also, it will treat with a passive system based on constructed wetlands the 
wastewater generated once the microorganisms that accumulate PHA are separated. 
BCM BCM is WP leader of WP 7 “Dissemination, commun ication and exploitation activities”. 
SES Validation of biopolymers produced at end-user level. The biopolymers will be tested in real manufactu ring chains in order 
to produce bags and films suitable for project target sectors.

3.4 
 Resources to be committed 
 
Below it is provided a more detailed description of  resources allocation for WP2 Conversion of OFMSW t o bioethanol as 
building block for the production of bioethylene, W P4 Biogas bioconversion to biomethane and added val ue products and WP8 
Project management 
  
- WP2:  Conversion of OFMSW to bioethanol as building block for the production of bioethylene  
 
IMECAL is the leader of WP2 and all the pilot plant  adaptation, new module building up and demonstrati on activities of Module 
1 of URBIOFIN biorefinery will be located in its bi otechnological demonstration plant (2000 m 
2). These activities will include the 
demonstration plant adaptation to improve the feasi bility and yield of bioethanol, to adapt the demons tration plant to new 
pretreatments, to adapt the plant to produce bioeth anol as building block, the integration of the bioe thanol-to-bioethylene unit 
and the development of a new monitoring system (Tasks 2.1. and 2.2). These activities require the involvement of engineers (1) 
technicians (2) and operators (4) in order to desig n and implement all the plant new modules (pre-trea tment, 20 m 3 hydrolysis 
reactor, 50 m 3 fermentation reactors, distillation units, and the installation of a new bioethanol-to-bioethylene operation unit). 
  
The demonstration activities planned in WP2 will be  carried out during 40 months of the project in a c ontinuous demonstration 
plant with the different raw materials defined in W P1 (Tasks 2.3, 2.4, 2.5). During the demonstration activities at semi-industrial 
scale, which will run in three-shift operation (24 hours a day), continuous results analysis (energy a nd mass balances, 
continuous process analysis (sugars, ethanol, inhib itors, etc), bioethanol yields, products characteri sations, quality controls, 
etc.) will be performed in order to carry out the appropriate redesign of activities, materials dosage, process control, with the aim 
to improve process performance. During all the demo nstration stage several human resources (3 engineer s, 3 technicians and 
5 operators) are needed to cover all activities for  the correct implementation of the project schedule . All IMECAL´s activities in 
WP2 will be carried out by own company personnel. 
 
- WP4:  Biogas bioconversion to biomethane and added value products.  
 
University of Valladolid will be the main responsib le for the design, construction, start-up and opera tion (including process 
monitoring) of 4 demo-scale technology set-ups in W P4 which includes: 1) 300 m 2 photobioreactor interconnected to a biogas 
scrubbing unit for biomethane production), 2) a 10 m 3 biotrickling filter coupled with a demo digestate n itrification unit (to supply 
the nitrate needed for the anoxic H 2S oxidation) for biogas desulfurization, 3) a 10 m 3 fermenter to bioconvert the H 2S-free 
biogas into biopolymers, including a biomass separa tion unit, 4) a gradual scale up to a 1 m 3 high mass transfer bioreactor for 
siloxane removal to polish biomethane. The 4 techno logies are intrinsically different in nature, purpo ses and monitoring needs, 
and will be run in continuous mode for 48 months at  the R&D center of URBASER in Zaragoza (Spain). The se activities, 
included in Tasks 4.1, 4.3 and 4.4, will require a large effort in term of person months from the 5 se nior researchers considered 
(1 full professor, 2 associate professors and 2 ass istant professors) for the design of the demo-biore actors (involving ATEX 
requirements due to the use of biogas as raw material), control strategies, process supervision and site visits. The construction, 
operation and monitoring of these industrial scale units will require the active participation of at l east 3 researchers and 1 
technician hired under the project basis. The monit oring of these 4 processes will involve the develop ment and validation of 
dedicated and time-consuming methodologies for the analysis of siloxanes, dynamics of microbial popula tion structure along 
the 4 year operation (using molecular biology techn iques) and physical/chemical and instrumental analy ses for the 
determination of the gas and liquid phase concentra tions of CH 4, CO 2, O 2, N 2, H 2S, N 2O, volatile organic compounds, NH 3, 
NH 4+, NO 3-, NO 2-, SO 42-, S 2O3-, S 2-, HS -, PO 43-, total organic carbon, inorganic carbon, TKN, Tota l Nitrogen, Total and Volatile 
suspended solids, pH, alkalinity, BOD, COD and poly hydroxyalkanoates. The large amount of data generat ed from the 
optimization of these 4 demo set-ups will also entail a significant effort in data analysis and report preparations.   
Associated with document Ref. Ares(2017)2272851 - 03/05/2017
                                                                             BBI 2016-D6

- WP8:  Project management  
 
IMECAL is URBIOFIN coordinator and responsible to m anage and assure the optimal implementation of this  large innovation-
action project (4 years duration; 16 consortium par tners, 4 advisory board members). This includes con tinuous reporting 
activities, administrative, financial and risk mana gement, progress monitoring and preparation of proj ects meetings and reports 
as well as the exploitation and innovation management.  
 
In addition to that, it is important to highlight that URBIOFIN project includes several modules that will be interconnected and the 
coordination of them will require specific proactiv e human resources which would address the potential  conflicts inherent to 
interrelated biorefinery technologies' projects. An  intensive coordination effort is needed in this po int in order to achive the 
project objectives. 
 
The project management requires exclusive staff ded icated to monitoring, quality control and project r isk control. This requires 
specific human resources to perform this control an d obtain a successful project result. In this task 2 people are going to be 
involved during all the project time.

PARTNER 1. Coordinator 
Name : Industrias Mecanicas Alcudia S.A. 
(IMECAL)  
Web page 
: www.imecal.com/perseo   
Type: SME  
Country: Spain 
 
Brief description of the organization:  
IMECAL is a SME which was founded in 1979 as an eng ineering company in the metal sector, working on de mand and 
manufacturing all type of metal-mechanical equipmen t for civil works, petro-refineries and petrochemic al, transportation, 
refrigeration industry, industrial auxiliary motor and ceramics industry, among others. R & D IMECAL D epartment has 
allowed the company to progress in the technological field, having made significant partnerships with companies, universities 
and public research organizations. The R&D line of production technology for second generation bioethanol has developed a 
biotechnological patented technology for obtaining bioethanol from Organic Municipal Waste. In 2007 IMECAL built a second 
generation bioethanol plant with a capacity to proc ess 25 ton/day of organic fraction of MSW (PERSEO B ioethanol®). Since 
this year IMECAL has participated in different proj ects to test and improve PERSEO technology to diffe rent MSW raw 
materials with different companies. IMECAL is member of the Biofuels TP Platform-European Union, and participates actively 
in several national and international conferences on biofuels.  
 
Role in the Project:   
IMECAL is the coordinator of URBIOFIN project. IMEC AL will lead WP2 regarding the conversion of OFMSW to bioethanol 
as building block for the production of bioethylene  , and will hold the corresponding demonstration ac tivities in its PERSEO 
semi-industrial plant. IMECAL will also participate  in WP1, WP3, WP5, WP6 and WP7, and will lead WP8 a s project 
manager.

PARTNER 2 
Name : ainia  
Web page 
: www.ainia.es  
Type: RTO  
Country: SPAIN  
Brief description of the organization:  
ainia is a RTD centre focused in the agro-food sect or and related industries. Nowadays, ainia has more than 700 food SME´s 
company members of its organization. The aim of the  centre is to promote research and technological de velopment in the 
agro-food sector, to increase quality in production , improve competitiveness and promote modernization and diversification in 
the agro-food industries. This is achieved providin g a wide range of technological services to its mem bers, through the 
execution of scientific research projects and technology transfer to the industry. ainia staff is composed by around 180 people.  
The work team involved in this project is formed by  Environmental Management researchers with wide experience in areas of 
activity related with the project: development of n ew biomass pre-treatments, alternative substrates a nd energy crops, 2-
stages fermentation, Anaerobic Digestion-biorefiner ies, VFA and nutrient recovery, reduction of biolog ical risks, digestate-
based fertilisers, control and modelling of the AD process and advanced microbial characterization.  
 
Role in the Project:  ainia will be focused in the development of two ph ase AD systems and in the VFA valorisation 
throughout the conversion of VFA to MCFA and later into PHA. Moreover it will participate in the valor isation of microalgae to 
biofertiliser. Ainia will participate in all WP, except WP2, and will lead WP1.  
Scientific team:   
Leticia REGUEIRO (F) as project coordinator in Ainia. She is PhD Chemica l Engineer and M.Sc. in Environmental and 
Chemical Engineering. She is specialist in the biom ethanation of agro-industrial waste through anaerob ic co-digestion. She 
has more than six years of experience in anaerobic digestion (AD) technologies with special focus in t he co-digestion 
strategies of organic wastes and the study of the m icrobial communities in the anaerobic reactors. Experience in participation 
and technical execution of diverse I+D projects and  technical assistances in the biogas field (ManureE comine Project, 
PROBIOGAS project, COMDIGEST project).  
Gracia SILVESTRE  (F) is PhD Chemical Engineer and has more than seven ye ars of experience in anaerobic digestion 
technologies with special focus in the co-digestion  strategies of organic wastes. Experience in partic ipation and technical 
execution of diverse R&D projects and technical ass istances in the biogas field. Experience in related  projects: SOSTRICE 
project (ongoing; she is involved in researching ac tivities related to demonstration plant testing), A D-WISE project (she was 
involved in calibration activities of the SVFA sens ors for optimized control of AD plants) and SLUDGE4 ENERGY project (she 
developed the pilot plant trials using a 2-phase anaerobic digestion pilot plant).  
Paz GÓMEZ (F)  is Agricultural Engineer, specialization on Rural Engineering, and has more than eight years of experience on 
the field of anaerobic digestion of agroindustrial waste, including agronomic valorisation of the digestate. Experience in related 
projects: BIOMAN project, focused on enzymatic and mechanical pretreatments to increase biogas product ion from 
lignocellulosic substrates (AD trials to test pretr eatments effect); DIGESMART project, focused on dig estate from manure 
recycling technologies (evaluation of the process of stripping), and AGROBIOMET project, focused on sustainable production 
and use of biomethane as vehicle fuel using manure and alternative biomasses (she was working on the AD pilot trials).  
Andrés PASCUAL (M)  is Agricultural Engineer with more than 15 years of work experience in R&D projects, with special 
focus on the optimisation of anaerobic digestion and digestate valorisation. Co-ordinator of the PROBIOGAS I+D project 
(2007-2011), which is a biogas key project in Spain with 30 partners and 9M€ budget. Consultant of IDAE (Ministry of Industry 
and Commerce of Spain) for biogas issues. Also co-ordinator of LIFE biogas related projects like INTEGRAL-B. He will 
supervise coordination of the AINIA team in the project as department leader.  
Alfredo RODRIGO (M).  PhD in Chemistry since 1996 and Agricultural Engin eer by the Technical University of Valencia 
(Spain). He works as project manager in AINIA since  1997 in the Department of Environment, Bioenergy a nd Industrial 
Hygiene. Senior expert with 5 years experience as researcher on groundwater pollution by agricultural activities and 18 years-
experienced on environment in food industry includi ng: environmental diagnosis, energy audits, life cy cle assessment and 
carbon footprint calculation of food companies and products and renewable energy technologies (biogas,  biodiesel,

Ainia’s infrastructure relevant to the proposed work: 
- Pilot biomethanation unit (72 batch digesters) to  carry out test of biogas potential (maximum biogas  potential according to 
VDI 4630 standard). 
- Continuous pilot biomethanation unit (15 digester s with 30 L working volume, 1 digester with 3 L wor king volume, 2-phase 
digester system: 10 L and 15 L working volume for e ach digester, 1 digester with 2 m 
3) to develop small scale digestion 
simulation. This facility makes possible the determ ination of yield and composition of biogas, optimum  composition of feed, 
optimum organic loading rate and digestate quality. 
- Chemical analysis, Chromatography laboratory, Microbiological analysis and molecular biology laboratory.  
- In ainia headquarters in Paterna (Valencia, Spain ), it is feasible to conduct workshops, training ac tivities as well as 
dissemination activities for an audience of 120 people

Name : URBASER S.A.

: http://www.urbaser.es/  
Type: Large Industry  
Country: SPAIN 
 
Brief description of the organization:  
URBASER belongs to the group ACS (“Actividades de C onstrucción y Servicios”), which is a worldwide ref erence in 
infrastructures, industrial services, energy and environment. 
The environmental company URBASER is leader in wast e management and treatment in Spain. It specializes  in street 
cleaning, waste removal and transporting, urban was te treatment and recycling, waste to energy facilit ies and 
comprehensive management of the water cycle and urban landscape and gardening.  
URBASER is the leader in removal and treatment of used mineral oils and treatment and removal of industrial waste.  
URBASER covers the entire value chain when providin g these services, from designing and conception, ca rrying out the 
project, construction, financing and operating a highly-qualified professional team.   
URBASER also operates in the field of renewable ene rgies with a view to limiting the negative impact o f greenhouse gases, 
for the purpose of which it is developing treatment processes for alternative sources of energy, biomass from biomass crops, 
waste woodland mass, biodegradable, agricultural and industrial waste. 
Urbaser achieved a business turnover of 1.498 milli on € in 2010 with a highly-qualified staff of more than 30.000 people and 
over 160 subsidiary companies forming the group. It  provides services to more than 50 million people a nd is active in 4 
continents. The main magnitudes are as follows:  
•   232 MW installed in renewable sources of energy, with a production of 479 GWh in 2010. 
•   Reducing CO 
2 production by more than 2.4 t/year. 
•   Treating and removing 4.6 million t/year of inert waste.  
•   Collecting and treating 150,000 t/year of industrial waste.  
•   Treating and regenerating 67,000 t/year of mineral oils. 
•   Annual removal of more than 5 million tons of solid urban waste. 
•   Annual cleaning of more than 8 million kilometers of streets. 
•   Annual maintenance of more than 60 million m² of green zones.

Role in the Project:   
URBASER will offer its R&D Center area to install n ew prototypes or pilot plants which allow the opera tion and validation of 
innovative technological solutions for the treatment of outlet streams coming from the fermentation process of municipal solid 
wastes, in order to get as much of high-grade valua ble products (biopolymers, biomethane, microalgae) and maximize the 
valorisation of the organic fraction of MSW (OFMSW) . In particular, URBASER will participate in the an aerobic digestion of 
OFMSW for VFA production and biogas production through methanogenic steps (WP3 leader, WP4), operating its anaerobic 
digester according to the project needs. Furthermor e, Urbaser will integrate of VFA, PHA production an d microalgae 
processes.  In addition to that, URBASER will participate in WP1, WP5, WP6, WP7 and WP8.

URBASER manages many waste treatment plants, equipp ed with varied technologies; consequently, it has a n experienced 
global vision of the different integrated technologies. At present, URBASER counts on a new Waste Technological Innovation 
R&D Center, called CIAM, focused on testing and studying innovative environmental technologies. This facility, located within 
a big industrial waste treatment plant, consists of different demonstration plants in the field of waste treatment (pre-treatment 
of municipal solid waste, anaerobic digestion of organic matter, composting, solid recovery fuel production and conversion of 
plastic waste into fuel). In addition to the pilot plants, a 250 m 2 testing bench surface at the R&D Center is also av ailable to 
install new prototypes or pilot plants; this testin g bench surface is equipped with the necessary util ities like compressed air, 
power supply, water, etc., a leachate collection sy stem and a modern laboratory to analyse samples in order to obtain vital 
information for R&D projects.

PARTNER 5 
Name : University of Valladolid

: www.uva.es; http://envtech.uva.es;  
http://gastreatment-

Type: RTO  
Country: SPAIN 
 
Brief description of the organization 
The Environmental Technology Group (EnvTech) from t he Department of Chemical Engineering and Environme ntal 
Technology at the University of Valladolid (UVa) st arted its research activities in the early 80s in t he treatment of industrial 
wastewaters and biological nutrient removal. Other research lines such as biological gas treatment, mi croalgae-based 
wastewater treatment and biomass valorization were initiated in 2000. Since 1980, the EnvTech has conducted a sustained 
and intense labour in the development of cost-effec tive technologies for pollution control in both was tewater and off-gas 
emissions. More than 35 years of expertise in desig n and operation of wastewater treatment processes, 16 of them related 
to microalgae-based wastewater treatment, biologica l gas treatment and microalgae valorization, suppor t the capacity of 
the group to conduct the tasks assigned in the URBi oFIN project, i.e. biogas upgrading to biomethane i n high rate algae 
ponds and subsequent biomass revalorization, biogas desulfurization by biotrickling filtration, removal of siloxanes from raw 
biogas and biogas conversion into high-added value products. Its research activity has been recognized  and financed 
within the frame of public R&D projects from the Spanish Ministry for Science and Education and the EU (42 projects with a 
total Budget of ≈5761000 € in the past 10 years). The research group has also collaborated with several companies aiming 
at reinforcing the mechanisms of knowledge transfer  between University and Industry (62 projects with a total Budget of 
≈7535000 € in the past 10 years). Nowadays, EnvTech  is composed of 2 full professors, 8 associate prof essors, 7 post-
docs, 15 PhD students and 5 technicians. In additio n, the academic and scientific productivity of the group during these 
past 5 years accounted for 15 PhD theses presented,  148 JCR articles, 4 patents and 150 contributions to International 
Congresses. 
 
Role in the Project:  
The EnvTech group will be involved in the upgrading  of raw biogas to biomethane in photobioreactors, t he selective 
removal of siloxanes from biomethane in two phase p artitioning bioreactors, the selective removal of H 2S from biogas and 
its further bioconversion into high-added value products such as PHAs. EnvTech will apply its 16 years  of R&D experience 
in the design and operation of algal-bacterial phot obioreactors to optimize the upgrading potential an d maximize the 
subsequent production of biobased products. The gro up has successfully operated both open and enclosed  
photobioreactors under indoor and outdoor condition s for the treatment of domestic and livestock waste waters. Besides, 
the broad experience of the EnvTech group in the operation of low-cost, high-efficiency bioreactors for waste gas treatment 
will be applied to the selective removal of siloxan es and H 
2S, and to the bioconversion of the raw biogas to hi gh-added 
value products. Role of EnvTech includes the participation in the following WPs: 1, 4 (leader), 6, 7 and 8.

Brief description of the organization:  
Exergy is one of the UK's leading renewable energy companies with the expertise to provide services, a cross the globe, to 
develop, engineer, construct and operate projects t hat contribute to our goal of a low carbon, sustain able future. We have 
been in the industry for over 10 years, contributin g to the development of the global renewable energy  market. We have 
helped to move the sustainable energy debate from t he margin to the mainstream. Operating across a ran ge of innovative 
low-carbon energy technologies, our capabilities cover everything from project inception to energy gen eration and operation. 
Sustainability lies at the core of our values; bala ncing commercial, environmental and social concerns to address the world’s 
energy problems is what makes us different. 
We are unique in our ability to offer vertically in tegrated skills in a range of sustainable energy te chnologies. Exergy can be 
involved at every stage: from project design and de velopment, through planning and financing, engineering and construction 
to operation. Exergy ensures schemes are designed a nd built to generate energy in the most economical way and with 
minimal environmental impact. 
Exergy provides a range of technical and profession al services across the chemical, energy and built e nvironment sector by 
means of a multi-disciplinary team supported by ext ensive practical experience in the following specia list areas: Feasibility 
Assessments that include techno-economic assessment s and LCC; Design, Modelling and Scaling up of Chem ical and 
Biochemical Processes; Resource Efficiency & Enviro nmental Management; Water Management Strategies; De sign and 
Delivery of Resource Efficiency support for SME’s; Development, Monitoring and Measurement of Sustaina bility Projects; 
Low Carbon footprint Construction Techniques and Li fe Cycle Assessment. Exergy has a strong work team made up of 
different profiles: chemical and process engineers,  mechanical engineers, civil engineers and environm ental engineers, 
amongst other. Exergy is also member of SPIRE and BIC. 
 
Role in the Project:  Exergy leads the WP6 where the entire urban proces s will be integrated and optimised through virtual 
simulations as well as the project’s impacts will be assessed (economic, environmental and social) along with the study of all 
the potential regulatory and legal aspects which mi ght impact on the project outcomes. Role of Exergy includes also the 
participation in the following WPs: 1, 7 and 8.

Name : Novozymes A/S

: www.novozymes.com

Industry  Country:

Brief description of the organization:  
Novozymes is a world leader in bio-innovation and s pecialised in industrial enzymes and microorganisms . NZ already 
markets over 700 biotechnology products in 130 coun tries.  The enzyme production leaves NZ with a glob al enzyme market 
share of 48% (2015). Around 14% of NZ revenue is sp ent on research and development, and it currently h olds almost 7,000 
granted or pending patents, which indicate the poss ibilities when nature and technology join forces. A s a leading biotech 
company, NZ believes that by using industrial biote chnology thousands of everyday products can potenti ally be re-
engineered to deliver enhanced sustainability perfo rmance, at no extra cost. Over the past 15 years, t he company has 
invested heavily in developing superior enzyme prod ucts to enable the biomass and MSW to bioethanol/bi ogas industry as 
well as the generation of simple sugars from lignoc ellulose for the bio-production of more advanced pr oducts. Novozymes is 
today supplying enzymes to the majority of existing lignocellulosic bio-ethanol plants. 
 
Role in the Project:   
Novozymes will sample enzyme products optimized for  degradation of MSW and provide recommendations for  optimization

Brief description of the organization:  
Wageningen University & Research (Wageningen UR) is  the umbrella organization comprising legal entitie s Wageningen 
University and Stichting Wageningen Research. The p artner entity is Wageningen Research. Wageningen UR  explores 
the potential of nature to improve the quality of l ife. With approximately 30 locations around the wor ld, 6,000 staff 
members and 9,000 students, Wageningen UR is a worl d leader in the biobased economy domain. An integra l way of 
working and cooperation between the exact sciences and the technological and social disciplines are th e key to its 
approach. Wageningen UR partners in developing chem icals, materials, fuels & energy that use biomass i nstead of fossil 
resources and in the creation and production of hea lthy and tasty food. Our in-depth knowledge on deve loping truly 
sustainable biomass valorisation chains (from raw m aterials through refining to marketable end-product s) for food and 
non-food applications drives our approach. Together with our customers, Wageningen UR develops production processes, 
biobased materials, and full sustainable biomass va lorisation strategies that will transform the curre nt economy into a 
sustainable bioeconomy. With innovative technologie s, Wageningen UR turns both primary crops and resid ues from the 
food industry, agriculture and natural infrastructu re into marketable products and energy: human food,  animal feed, 
chemicals, materials, fuels, power and heat. The In stitute Food & Biobased Research (FBR) will represe nt Wageningen 
Research in this project with its fermentation and microalgae expertise in microbial production of med ium chain-length 
(mcl) fatty acids and PHA’s and development of industrial applications for these components. 
Role in the Project: 
Wageningen UR will establish fermentation processes using Cryptococcus sp . for medium-chain fatty acid (MCFA) based 
on the existing volatile fatty acid (VFA) stream an d will establish a fermentation process for medium- chain length poly-
hydroxy alkanoate (mcl-PHA) production using the MCFA’s as substrate and exiting mixed cultures and/or pure cultures of 
Pseudomonas putida  as production organism. Role of Wageningen UR incl udes the participation in WPs 1, 3, 5, 6, 7 and 
8.

Brief description of the organization:  
CIEMAT (Centro de Investigaciones Energéticas, Medi oambientales y Tecnológicas) is a Public Research I nstitution 
depending on the Spanish Ministry of Economy and Co mpetitiveness. Main objectives of CIEMAT are to pro mote and 
execute research, innovation and technical developm ent in the energy sector. CIEMAT research is conduc ted in 
cooperation with other institutions and organisatio ns in joint R&D&I projects, providing specialized t echnical services, 
education and training. Ciemat´s employees are arou nd 1,326 people, technologically and geographically  diversified in 
several research Centres in Spain, with central offices and a great part of the facilities located in Madrid. 
The Biofuels Unit is attached to the Renewable Ener gies Department of CIEMAT, whose and the main objec tive is to 
perform R&D projects in the renewable energies area , both in resources evaluation and conversion techn ology 
development. The Biofuels Unit performs R&D projects in the area of bioconversion processes to transform lignocellulosic 
biomass into bioproducts and biofuels such as bioet hanol, by means of efficient and low cost biotechno logical routes, 
facilitating that these processes can be adopted by  industry. The team is composed of scientists such as analytic 
chemists, biochemists, and microbiologists, with sp ecialization in the different areas involved in the  biotechnological 
conversion of lignocellulose into bioproducts and bioethanol. 
In the last years, significant advances in the diff erent steps of the conversion process, i.e., pretre atment, enzymatic 
hydrolysis, and yeast fermentation have been attain ed, based on large research activity on different l ignocellulosic 
materials. It hasThose advances allowed the team ad dressing the use of lignocellulose in a wider appro ach in order to 
obtain a sugar platform and valuable streams for th e production of a variety of bioproduct/biofuels, w ithin the biorefinery 
concept. The experience of the group members is shown by the publications and granted projects achieved.  
 
Role in the Project: 
CIEMAT will be focused on adapting/improving the PE RSEO bioethanol production process to the new feeds tock by 
optimizing pretreatment, enzymatic hydrolysis and f ermentation steps. Apart from sugar recovery and et hanol yield, 
energy efficiency ratio, mass balance and toxic com pounds generation will be used for the estimation o f the optimized 
parameters. CIEMAT will also assist IMECAL in the a nalysis of the fractions generated in the demo tria ls. Role of 
CIEMAT includes the participation in WPs 1, 2, 5, 6, 7 and 8. 
Scientific team:   
Dr. Mercedes Ballesteros (F)  is Head of the Biofuels Unit at CIEMAT since 2000.  She is Ph.D. in Biology by the 
Autonoma University and Master in Biotechnology by Complutense University of Madrid and has more than 30 years’ 
experience in the field of biomass utilization by b iological processes for energy purposes, mainly in developing 
technologies to produce bioethanol from lignocellul osic biomass. She has authored about 90 papers and 5 chapters in 
technical books and is co-author of 3 patents.  
Dr. Ignacio Ballesteros (M)  is a Senior Researcher at the Biofuels Unit of CIE MATand obtained his PhD degree in 
Biology at the University of Alcalá de Henares in 2 000. He has large expertise in biological processes  for biomass 
valorization in the field of enzymatic hydrolysis and fermentation as well as in biomass pre-treatment, developinghis entire 
research career within the Department of Energy's R enewable Energy Unit atCIEMAT. He is co-author of 3 5 scientific 
papers and co-inventor of 2 patents. 
Dr. José Miguel Oliva Domínguez  (M) , Senior Researcher at Biofuels Unit of Ciemat. He has a PhD in Biology by

Brief description of the organization:  
VISUM is an optical engineering company from Dublin  that specializes in the development and commercial ization of Near 
Infrared Spectroscopy (NIRS)-based portable and inl ine analyzers and measurement systems for process m onitoring and 
quality control applications in the food, pharmaceutical and chemical applications. The company was established in 2014 and 
currently employs 9 staff from its facilities in Nexus UCD (technology park at the University College Dublin campus). In 2016, 
the company launched the VISUMPalm (a handheld NIR measurement instrument) and has secured first sales . An 
integration platform (VisumNIR) for the inline version is currently under development in cooperation with early adopter clients 
from the food processing industry (dairy, meat and olive oil) and pharmaceutical industries. VISUM Ltd . is an SME 
Champion-awarded a Phase 1 and a subsequent Phase 2 Grant under H2020’s SME Instrument.  
Role in the Project:   
VISUM will participate in WP2 where they will test novel advanced sensors for monitoring selected proc ess parameters and 
will integrate them at plant level together with a bespoke control system. They will also collaborate in the study of the relevant 
parameters to be analysed in order to select the most suitable sensor technologies.  
VISUM will also develop data mining tools to produc e relevant decision support tools for optimally con trolling production 
based on relevant process data.  
VISUM will also participate in WP1, supporting the work on preliminary actions for biorefinery design which will feed into 
WP2.  
VISUM will also take part in WP6, in the environmen tal, economic and regulatory assessments from the m onitoring at plant 
scale point of view and will participate in WP7 by actively engaging in exploitation and dissemination  tasks. Role of VISUM 
includes the participation in WPs 5 and 8.

Brief description of the organization: 
Natureplast Company was founded in December 2006 and is specialized in supporting bioplastics applications development 
through its activities:  
• Raw materials  distribution: hundreds of different references of biobased and / or biodegradable materials (PLA, PHA s, 
PBS, starch based materials, etc.) available with worldwide network.  
• Services such as project engineering, technical support, technical survey, training, etc.  
• And Research & Development  through its 100% owned daughter company Biopolynov: our compounding facility allows 
us to develop and produce compounds with improved properties depending of our customers and applications needs. 
The company’s works usually concerns improving mech anical, processing or thermal properties through th e use of several 
raw materials, additives, natural fibers, nanofillers or by-products (or wastes) from different industries.  
In summary, the goal is to help industry to put bio plastics end-products into the market through our a ccess to raw materials 
and our capacity to develop specific compounds with improved properties.  
 
Natureplast and Biopolynov teams are working for ye ars in bioplastics modification and properties impr ovement. The team 
gained a strong experience in R&D on bioplastics wh ich permit Biopolynov to answer the best to the cus tomers’ needs. 
Natureplast also has the widest raw material portfo lio in Europe and has access to almost all kind of bioplastics and 
additives all around the world.  
Biopolynov has a strong knowledge in the developmen t and production of bioplastics compounds at small industrial scale 
(from 1 to 50 kg). An industrial production line (200 kg/h) is planned to be bought by the end of 2017. 
 
Role in the Project:

and to modify them to improve their processability and properties for the targeted applications. 
Role of Natureplast includes the participation in WPs 1, 5, 6, 7 and 8.

Brief description of the organization:  
The Regional Institute of Castilla-La Mancha for Ag ri-Food and Forest Research and Development (IRIAF) , which belongs 
to the Ministry of Agriculture and Environment of t he Regional Government of Castilla-La Mancha (JCCM) , consists of 6 
different research centres. It developed the CLAMBE R Project (Castilla-La Mancha Bio-Economy Region Pr oject) and has

and forest sectors.  
Thanks to this Project, which was co-funded with ER DF through the Ministry of Economy and Competitiven ess of the 
National Government of Spain (MINECO), the CLAMBER Plant was built in 2015. It is a public demonstrati ve biorefinery at 
the service of companies and dedicated to scientifi c research, scale-up experiments and development of  new processes 
and high value products from lignocellulosic and fermentable biomass, both residual and cultivated.  
 
Role in the Project:  IRIAF will be in charge of the VFA valorisation th roughout the conversion of VFA to MCFA and later

3). Also, it will treat with a passive system based on constructed 
wetlands the wastewater generated once the microorg anisms that accumulate PHA are separated. Role of I RIAF includes 
the participation in WPs 1, 3, 6, 7 and 8.

CLAMBER. Castilla La

To create a technologically advanced 
biorefinery pilot plant that allows the 
research on production of innovative
